               <i class="Icon Fw-n Va-t" style="color:#ffffff;height:40px;line-height:40px;font-size:16px;">
                
               </i>
              </a>
              <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
              </div>
              <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:9px;border-left-width:8px;border-right-width:8px;border-color:#e7e7e7 transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483646;top:29px;left:50%;margin-left:-8px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
              </div>
              <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="position:absolute;overflow:hidden;margin-top:-3px;margin-left:0px;top:40px;left:auto;right:-11.5px;display:inline-block;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
               <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">

           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-118947357139">
                      This Tiny Spanish Town Uses Twitter to Run Everything, and Its Working
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-118947357139" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                            <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="http://www.digitaltrends.com" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                             Andy Boxall, Digital Trends
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             May 14, 2015
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-118947357139" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <img alt="This Tiny Spanish Town Uses Twitter to Run Everything, and Its Working" height="600" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg" width="900"/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          If you use Twitter, then youll know its an interesting, if often frivolous social network. However, did you realize that when managed correctly, it could be used to run a small town? Thats whats happening in
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.ayuntamientojun.org/index.php/directorio" target="_blank">
                           Jun, Spain
                          </a>
                          , where
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://twitter.com/AyuntamientoJUN" target="_blank">
                           Twitter
                          </a>
                          is the main way the government communicates with the people who live there, and vice versa.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Jun is home to 3,500 people, and Twitter is used since September 2011 to spread everything from local news and developments, to job opportunities and the latest school dinner menus by the local government. On the other side, Jun residents will book appointments with doctors, lodge complaints about local services, report crimes, and generally become involved in the local community.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Related:
                          </b>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.digitaltrends.com/social-media/twitter-reaches-300-million-active-users-investor-expectations-not-met/" target="_blank">
                           Twitter now has 300 million users
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Its not just about basic communication either. Mayor Rodriguez Salas is frequently active though
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://twitter.com/JoseantonioJun" target="_blank">
                           his own account
                          </a>
                          . All the towns public services have their own Twitter account, as does the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://twitter.com/PoliciaJUN" target="_blank">
                           police force
                          </a>
                          , even though there is only one police officer. The squad car has the Twitter account painted on the body, and seemingly everywhere one looks, the Twitter bird logo can be seen. Even the guy who drives the street sweeper is a Twitter user, and is known for his
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://twitter.com/BarredoraJun" target="_blank">
                           cheery and amusing messages
                          </a>
                          , which he posts along with before and after shots of his best work.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Does any of this social networking make a difference to the way Jun operates? According to a report published by
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f0ba40e2-e2d2-369f-b52c-f54bca54beca;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/gadgets-and-tech/features/the-town-that-runs-on-twitter-juns-residents-tweet-to-report-crime-and-chat-to-their-mayor-10248167.html" target="_blank">
                           The Independent
                          </a>
                          , things work very well. It gives the example of a resident tweeting a photo showing a broken streetlamp, which was repaired three-and-a-half minutes later. Thats faster than it would take many of us to change a bulb in our own homes. Jun doesnt leave its older citizens out of all this either, and has a special program for those over 65 years old to learn about social media and how to use the Internet.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The mayor is says Twitter helps bring residents and government closer together, and that where before town employees werent recognized for work in the community, are now appreciated, which means people take more pride in their work. Law enforcement also benefits from an improved image, and can react faster thanks to reports coming through faster, and usually with photos that include the exact location.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Researchers at MITs Laboratory for Social Machines are now studying Jun and its method of virtual governance  which is believed to be the only one of its type in the world  to see if the project can be implemented on a larger scale elsewhere.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="article-bottom-share-buttons-118947357139" style="display:inline-block;">
                      <div class="Mb-30 Mt-40 Cl-b W-100" style="-webkit-user-select:none;cursor:default;-webkit-tap-highlight-color:rgba(0,0,0,0);z-index:2;text-align:center;white-space:nowrap;">

w250\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":250,"height":133,"size_type":"250","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":300,"height":160,"size_type":"300","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w350\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":350,"height":187,"size_type":"350","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w400\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":400,"height":213,"size_type":"400","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w450\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":450,"height":240,"size_type":"original","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w450\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":450,"height":240,"size_type":"450","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FiblWPF8xy5P9yZU9v_eDVh0FlAk","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F41.media.tumblr.com\u002F9ca379c15e6063a191959509d18dd49c\u002Ftumblr_inline_nrfwpdgURc1r19dv9_540.png"}],"highlight_color":"#ffffff","data_version":"1","title":"Does Googles Ad Network Discriminate Against Women?","summary":"A new paper by researchers at Carnegie Mellon and the International Computer Science Institute suggests that Google's ad network may have inadvertently discriminated against women seeking jobs.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Ffcd80f459c21828b0bcf5a2f28455606b1d08437.png\" alt=\"Does Google&#x2019;s Ad Network Discriminate Against Women?\" width=\"500\" height=\"357\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGoogle&#x2019;s motto is &#x201C;Don&#x2019;t be evil,&#x201D; and one could argue that for the most part, it has lived up to that goal. But a new study says that the algorithm behind the company&#x2019;s ad-targeting network may be inadvertently discriminating against women.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Farxiv.org\u002Fpdf\u002F1408.6491v2.pdf\"\u003Enew paper published by researchers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E from Carnegie Mellon University and the International Computer Science Institute &#x2014; originally \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.technologyreview.com\u002Fnews\u002F539021\u002Fprobing-the-dark-side-of-googles-ad-targeting-system\u002F\"\u003Ereported by MIT Technology Review\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;&#x2014;&#xA0;looked at ads served up on third-party websites using Google&#x2019;s ad network.&#xA0;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt found that when users identified themselves as males, the ad network was more likely to display an advertisement on the site for a career-coaching agency promising executive positions offering $200,000 salaries. Female users, on the other hand, were more likely to see ads for a &#x201C;generic job posting service and an auto dealer.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003EHow did they figure this out?\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe researchers discovered the disparity using a program called AdFisher, which simulates users&#x2019; Web-browsing habits. They then used \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.google.com\u002Fsettings\u002Fu\u002F0\u002Fads\u002Fauthenticated\"\u003EGoogle&#x2019;s Ads Settings tool\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;&#x2014; a service that lets you control the kinds of ads you see based on your demographic and browsing habits &#x2014; to set the gender of the simulated user to either male or female.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"460\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F4b061eacdff4b7d4de862733b76f55540b15a268.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPrior to performing the test, they made sure the only difference between the male and female simulated users was their gender. All other browsing habits and demographics were the same.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUsing AdFisher, they had 500 simulated male users and 500 simulated female users browse the same job-hunting sites. The researchers then had the same simulated users visit the Times of India&#x2019;s website, where the career-coaching ad appeared.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"500\" height=\"323\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fe76ee12b51c053ea4e9e9ab4399dde2c53b84c5e.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Barrett Group of Warwick, R.I., placed the career-coaching ads shown mostly to men in these tests.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen the testing was completed, AdFisher found that the simulated male users saw significantly more ads for the career-coaching service than the simulated females. The males were shown the ad 1,852 times, while the women were shown it just 318 times.\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003EAnd that could have some legal implications &#x2014; including potential inquiries from the Federal Trade Commission to determine whether discriminatory practices were at play.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003EWhat&#x2019;s an advertising algorithm?\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA key question in this conversation, though, is whether&#xA0;the advertiser chose to target ads for the career-coaching service at men, or if Google&#x2019;s ad-serving software was at fault. To figure that out, it helps to know how Google&#x2019;s ad network serves up ads.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt starts when a website like the Times of India signs up with Google to place ads on its site. Advertisers participating in Google&#x2019;s ad network tell Google the kinds of consumers they want to reach with their ads.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to Google, advertisers can specify a multitude of parameters for consumers they want to market to, including the types of websites they visit, their age, general interests, and, of course, gender.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E&#x201C;\u003C\u002Fi\u003EAdvertisers can choose to target the audience they want to reach, and we have \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fsupport.google.com\u002Fadwordspolicy\u002Fanswer\u002F143465?hl=en\"\u003Epolicies\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that guide the type of interest-based ads that are allowed,&#x201D; a spokesperson for Google told us.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We provide transparency to users with &#x2018;Why This Ad&#x2019; notices and Ads Settings, as well as the ability to opt out of interest-based ads.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen you visit a website that participates in Google&#x2019;s ad network, Google detects the kind of consumer you are based on your profile and matches you with the appropriate ad.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"500\" height=\"423\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F2202505f4ddb97cc6a64c5b4ff6b36437529985a.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor example, if you&#x2019;re a 30-year-old man who likes to visit sports and gaming sites, Google&#x2019;s ad network will recognize that and probably show you an ad for a new video game or sporting event. Google&#x2019;s algorithms can also calculate who&#x2019;s more likely to click on a specific ad. The more people who click on ads served up by Google, the more money the company and the website publisher make; that means Google is more likely to show ads that have a high click-through rate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003EHow could this be discrimination?\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor the most part, advertisers are allowed to target specific gender demographics for certain products. For instance, a company selling maternity clothing is completely within its rights to target women in a certain age group who have visited pregnancy-related websites.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe problem starts when you are advertising for something called \u003Ci\u003Epublic accommodations\u003C\u002Fi\u003E,\u003Ci\u003E \u003C\u002Fi\u003Esays UC Berkeley law professor David Oppenheimer.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;You can&#x2019;t say you&#x2019;re offering a service and restrict it based on gender, or race, or any other protected characteristics,&#x201D; Oppenheimer explained. But he added that this would apply only if the services were purposely being targeted at men rather than women.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBecause the researchers were unable to find out whether the advertiser was specifically targeting men &#x2014; or to get Google to reveal how its algorithm works &#x2014; they were unable to determine whether women were being deliberately excluded from seeing the career-coaching ad.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe reached out to the Barrett Group for comment but did not receive one by presstime.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EStill, the ad network&#x2019;s apparent exclusion of female users could be considered an \u003Ci\u003Eadverse impact&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003Eform of discrimination,&#xA0;Oppenheimer explained\u003Ci\u003E.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAdverse impact discrimination happens when companies attempt to do something completely benign but end up inadvertently discriminating against a group.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOppenheimer points to an example of a city specifying a height requirement for bus drivers due to the size of the driver&#x2019;s seat. If the height requirement is too great, it would naturally eliminate a disproportionate number of women from being able to hold the job. And that is illegal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"450\" height=\"240\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w450\u002F2ac29dd509f7cd7b065ff36d0b37f23287bbad81.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn the case of Google&#x2019;s ad network, the algorithm that ensures it places ads on sites based on what users are more likely to click on could have inadvertently decided that men would click the link for the career-coaching service more frequently than women. As a result, it would have shown the ad to more men, thus putting women at a disadvantage.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to Oppenheimer, if the algorithm turns out to be the cause of the disparity, a government regulatory agency such as the Equal Employment Opportunity Commission or the Department of Justice Civil Rights Division could step in and work to ensure the issue is addressed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition, an individual or a group could bring a class action suit against Google or its advertisers seeking injunctive relief. The company or its advertisers could also face possible punitive damages.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor what it&#x2019;s worth, the authors of the study aren&#x2019;t accusing Google or its ad partners of deliberately keeping women out of high-paying jobs. They do, however, call for greater transparency in the way ads are selected for individual users.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We would remain concerned if the cause of the discrimination was an algorithm run by Google, or if the advertiser automatically determined\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003Ethat males are more likely than females to click on the ads in question,&#x201D; the researchers wrote.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The amoral status of an algorithm does not negate its effects on Reportedly Testing a Human-Powered Digital Assistant Named Moneypenny\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFacebook is reportedly testing a personal assistant service built into its Messenger app and referred to internally as &#x201C;Moneypenny&#x201D; &#x2014; the name of the secretary from the \u003Ci\u003EJames Bond\u003C\u002Fi\u003E franchise. According to a report \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.theinformation.com\u002Fcoming-soon-to-facebook-messenger-moneypenny-assistant\"\u003Efrom \u003Ci\u003EThe Information\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, Moneypenny is not a virtual entity in the vein of Microsoft&#x2019;s Cortana or Apple&#x2019;s Siri, but a service that connects users to &#x201C;real people&#x201D; to help with &#x201C;researching and ordering products and services, among other tasks.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis description suggests that Moneypenny is closer to a traditional concierge system than the recent breed of digital personal assistants.&#xA0;A number of companies have targeted this space recently including&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgetmagicnow.com\u002F\"\u003EMagic\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a US startup that puts users in touch with &#x201C;trained operators&#x201D; via text message, allowing them to order anything from takeaway to flights at any hour of the day. Other rivals include&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Foperator.com\u002F\"\u003EOperator\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (a project run by&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.fastcompany.com\u002F3045390\u002Ffast-feed\u002Fthe-operator-app-wants-to-make-online-shopping-less-like-online-shopping\"\u003Ean Uber cofounder and a former Zynga executive\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) and&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.gobutlernow.com\u002Findex.php?country=UK&amp;language=en\"\u003EGoButler\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (a clone of Magic with international reach).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not clear how developed Moneypenny is or when the product could be launched (it&#x2019;s currently being tested internally by the social network&#x2019;s employees, says \u003Ci\u003EThe Information\u003C\u002Fi\u003E), but Facebook has already shown it&#x2019;s determined to build new services into Messenger. Since splitting the messaging service&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2014\u002F4\u002F9\u002F5598440\u002Ffacebook-will-turn-off-messaging-in-its-mobile-app-forcing-you-to-download-messenger\"\u003Eaway from its main app last April\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the company has been developing Messenger into a fully-fledged platform to rival Asian services like WeChat and LINE, apps that combine commerce and gaming with chatting.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn recent months, Facebook has added&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2015\u002F5\u002F20\u002F8629187\u002Ffacebook-messenger-video-calls-global-roll-out\"\u003Evideo calling \u003C\u002Fa\u003Eand a&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2015\u002F3\u002F17\u002F8235781\u002Ffacebook-messanger-payments-send-receive-money\"\u003Epayments service\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to Messenger, as well as launching&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2015\u002F4\u002F8\u002F8371349\u002Ffacebook-messenger-web-browsers-now-available\"\u003Ea version for the app for web browsers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. There are&#xA0;also rumors that&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2015\u002F5\u002F18\u002F8620133\u002Ffacebook-messenger-games-development-report\"\u003Egames for the app\u003C\u002Fa\u003E are in the works. It&#x2019;s not too surprising then for Facebook to explore the digital assistant arena, and connecting users to real people is presumably less hassle than building a virtual assistant from scratch.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from theverge.com:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca e":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":500,"height":500,"size_type":"500","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fcb1e200a967315c6f4e8d83120f2a4f49104c92e.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":540,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FBKIvhhXFxFBWvY_IuxZbXoM-EEE","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F36.media.tumblr.com\u002F33b79d50e347d8dad8dd818abdfc114a\u002Ftumblr_inline_nrgc6dxhiM1r794yr_540.jpg"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"5 Ways Amazon Has Changed the Web  for Good and Bad","summary":"Over the last 20 years Amazon has changed many of the rules governing the online world, including some of the rules enacted in Washington, DC. Here are five key issues where Amazon used its massive power to sway the market in one direction or another.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fcb1e200a967315c6f4e8d83120f2a4f49104c92e.jpg\" alt=\"5 Ways Amazon Has Changed the Web &#x2014; for Good and Bad\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn Wednesday, I bought an umbrella at a Web site. I was utterly confident it would arrive on Friday, even though hadn&#x2019;t paid any express shipping fees. Thank you, Amazon Prime.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMaking transcontinental logistics boringly predictable is just one of the dents Amazon has left in the digital universe over the past two decades. The Web&#x2019;s biggest retailer (if also one of its \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fycharts.com\u002Fcompanies\u002FAMZN\u002Fprofit_margin\"\u003Eleast-profitable\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;firms) celebrates its 20th birthday on Wednesday. Over that period Amazon has changed many of the rules governing the online world &#x2014; including some of the rules enacted in Washington, DC.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome of those changes &#x2014; like the ability to make near-thoughtless purchases of random stuff from anywhere with an Internet connection &#x2014; are truly awesome. Others, not so much. Here are five key issues where Amazon used its massive power to sway the market, or chose to sit on the sidelines.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E1. Digital rights management: Playing both sides\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe shift of music, movies, TV, and books from physical to digital has been one the biggest stories in technology over the last two decades. And, at an important moment, Amazon helped push that transition in a customer-friendly direction.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough it didn&#x2019;t beat Apple to selling major-label music without digital rights management restrictions, it \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fvoices.washingtonpost.com\u002Ffasterforward\u002F2007\u002F09\u002Famazons_mp3_store.html\"\u003Elaunched a DRM-free music store in September of 2007\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a year and a half before \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fvoices.washingtonpost.com\u002Ffasterforward\u002F2009\u002F04\u002Fthe_drm_era_ends_for_itunes_mu.html\"\u003EApple got out of selling DRMed music\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. That was both good for business (it got Amazon ahead of a trend) and good for buyers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlas, we haven&#x2019;t seen the same positive outcome from other forms of digital media. Amazon&#x2019;s&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FInstant-Video\u002Fb?ie=UTF8&amp;node=2858778011\"\u003EInstant Video streaming catalog\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which includes some great exclusives like the Washington send-up &#x201C;Alpha House,&#x201D; is a great bonus for Prime subscribers and a key cord-cutting tool. But Amazon&#x2019;s video downloads come as locked with DRM as everybody else&#x2019;s.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo do most of the titles on \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FKindle-eBooks\u002Fb?ie=UTF8&amp;node=154606011\"\u003EAmazon&#x2019;s Kindle Store\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.washingtonpost.com\u002Fe-book-business-should-take-a-page-from-music-industry-and-go-drm-free\u002F2011\u002F04\u002F05\u002FAFBRbG1C_story.html\"\u003Edoesn&#x2019;t even indicate when an author or publisher has opted out of DRM\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. (Most publishers don&#x2019;t take that option, even though insisting on DRM that ties e-book downloads to Amazon&#x2019;s apps only \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.project-disco.org\u002Fcompetition\u002F071013-price-fixing-wont-open-the-e-books-market-but-dumping-drm-just-might\u002F\"\u003Eincreases the etailer&#x2019;s market power &#x2014; something book publishers constantly whine about.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn the upside, DRM&#x2019;s dominance in e-books makes physical books look that much more flexible and permanent. This may factor into \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.slate.com\u002Farticles\u002Fbusiness\u002Fthe_edgy_optimist\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Findependent_bookstores_rising_they_can_t_compete_with_amazon_and_don_t_have.html\"\u003Ethe surprising resurgence of independent bookstores\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E2. Internet sales tax: The big switcheroo\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor years, Amazon had a one-word answer to proposals that it start collecting state sales taxes shoppers owe on their purchases: No. Make that three words: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.slate.com\u002Farticles\u002Ftechnology\u002Ftechnology\u002F2011\u002F07\u002Famazon_wants_to_save_you_money.html\"\u003ENo, No, and No\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. In 2011, it even \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.dallasnews.com\u002Fbusiness\u002Fheadlines\u002F20110210-amazon.com-shutting-irving-office-over-tax-dispute.ece\"\u003Eclosed a warehouse in Texas\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2014;yes, that hive of socialist income redistribution&#x2014;when presented with a bill for sales taxes due.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut later that year, Amazon started changing its mind, signing deals with a growing number of states to collect sales taxes. In return, it was allowed to open warehouses in those states, speeding up its distribution. The company now even backs \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fmarketplacefairness.org\u002Fsupport\u002F\"\u003Efederal legislation to mandate sales-tax collection by online retailers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe group that once worked with Amazon against these state-level sales-tax efforts is annoyed at the change and thinks Amazon is now out to burden smaller competitors.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Remember 20 years ago when everyone was worked up about big-box stores killing family-run businesses?&#x201D; wrote Katie McAuliffe, executive director of digital liberty at \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fatr.org\"\u003EAmericans for Tax Reform\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;Now that Amazon itself is a big-boxer, it&#x2019;s in league with crushing small businesses.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E3. Privacy: Mostly silent\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn many other issues, Amazon has been much less vocal than you might expect, considering its size and influence. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EConsider the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.project-disco.org\u002Fprivacy\u002F120312-ecpa-and-the-high-cost-of-tech-short-sightedness\u002F\"\u003Epathetically weak laws about government access to communications stored online\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Amazon joined a group lobbying for their reform, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.digitaldueprocess.org\u002Findex.cfm?objectid=DF652CE0-2552-11DF-B455000C296BA163\"\u003Ethe Digital Due Process\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnet.com\u002Fnews\u002Fapple-dropbox-join-electronic-privacy-act-fight\u002F\"\u003Ebefore Apple and Dropbox\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. But it&#x2019;s been mostly silent since and only got around to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fwhy-its-exciting-news-that-verizon-and-at-t-are-no-72240131435.html\"\u003Ethe basic step of posting a &#x201C;transparency report&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E inventorying government data requests \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fd0.awsstatic.com\u002Fcertifications\u002FTransparency_Report.pdf\"\u003Ethis year.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It hasn&#x2019;t been nearly as active as others on surveillance issues,&#x201D; summed up Mike Masnick, founder of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftechdirt.com\"\u003ETechdirt tech-policy blog\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E4. Patents: A troll model\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn patents, Amazon has arguably been part of the problem more than the solution. It secured \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpatft.uspto.gov\u002Fnetacgi\u002Fnph-Parser?Sect1=PTO1&amp;Sect2=HITOFF&amp;d=PALL&amp;p=1&amp;u=%2Fnetahtml%2FPTO%2Fsrchnum.htm&amp;r=1&amp;f=G&amp;l=50&amp;s1=5960411.PN.&amp;OS=PN\u002F5960411&amp;RS=PN\u002F5960411\"\u003Ea patent on its &#x201C;1-click&#x201D; shopping interface\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, then promptly sued Barnes &amp; Noble for infringing on what the pioneering Internet publisher \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.oreilly.com\u002Fpub\u002Fpr\u002F537\"\u003ETim O&#x2019;Reilly called &#x201C;a parody&#x201D; of an invention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (and which the European Union \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theregister.co.uk\u002F2011\u002F07\u002F07\u002Feuropean_patent_office_says_amazon_oneclick_payment_too_obvious_to_patent\u002F\"\u003Ehas yet to find worthy of a patent\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd while Amazon&#x2019;s far smaller rival NewEgg.com has spent millions of its own dollars battling patent trolls in court, Amazon has shown nowhere near the same resistance to that form of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fwhy-the-tech-industry-hates-patent-trolls-and-you-121628489339.html\"\u003Elegalized extortion\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. In one case, it \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.seattletimes.com\u002Fbusiness\u002Famazoncom-set-to-pay-on-patents\u002F\"\u003Epaid $40 million\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to license a bogus patent that \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Farstechnica.com\u002Ftech-policy\u002F2013\u002F01\u002Fhow-newegg-crushed-the-shopping-cart-patent-and-saved-online-retail\u002F\"\u003ENewEgg later had thrown out in court\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E5. Net neutrality: Mostly neutered\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBerin Szoka, president of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftechfreedom.org\"\u003ETechFreedom\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, noted that Amazon had pushed early on for legislative protection of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fhow-comcast-verizon-and-the-rest-of-big-telecom-112519949724.html\"\u003Enet neutrality\u003C\u002Fa\u003E but allowed that its support was &#x201C;tepid.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpublicknowledge.org\"\u003EPublic Knowledge\u003C\u002Fa\u003E counsel Harold Feld doesn&#x2019;t agree with Szoka on too many things but did on that one, writing that &#x201C;Amazon has been much more interested in keeping a low profile than in showing leadership.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAll of this stands in striking contrast to the conduct of the man who has benefited most from Amazon, founder Jeff Bezos. He has plowed his \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bloomberg.com\u002Fbillionaires\u002Fprofile\u002Fjeff-bezos\"\u003Ebillions in personal wealth\u003C\u002Fa\u003E into a variety of projects without an immediate or obvious reward, from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.washingtonpost.com\u002Fnational\u002Fwashington-post-to-be-sold-to-jeff-bezos\u002F2013\u002F08\u002F05\u002Fca537c9e-fe0c-11e2-9711-3708310f6f4d_story.html\"\u003Ebuying my old employer the Washington Post\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bezosexpeditions.com\u002F\"\u003Efinancing underwater archeology\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and launching a private space program, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blueorigin.com\u002F\"\u003EBlue Origin\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAny one of those ventures may fare no better than Amazon&#x2019;s Fire Phone. But combined, they cast a some favorable light on the company whose success made them possible. I guess they do make me feel better about all the money I&#x2019;ve sunk into Amazon over the past two decades.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEmail \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca Tiny Spanish Town Uses Twitter to Run Everything, and Its Working","summary":"If you use Twitter, then youll know its an interesting, if often frivolous social network.  Jun is home to 3,500 people, and Twitter is used since September 2011 to spread everything from local news and developments, to job opportunities and the latest school dinner menus by the local government.  Related: Twitter now has 300 million users Its not just about basic communication either.  Mayor Rodriguez Salas is frequently active though his own account.","body":"\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w900\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg\" alt=\"This Tiny Spanish Town Uses Twitter to Run Everything, and It&#x2019;s Working\" width=\"900\" height=\"600\"\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you use Twitter, then you&#x2019;ll know it&#x2019;s an interesting, if often frivolous social network. However, did you realize that when managed correctly, it could be used to run a small town? That&#x2019;s what&#x2019;s happening in \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ayuntamientojun.org\u002Findex.php\u002Fdirectorio\"\u003EJun, Spain\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, where \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002FAyuntamientoJUN\"\u003ETwitter\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is the main way the government communicates with the people who live there, and vice versa.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJun is home to 3,500 people, and Twitter is used since September 2011 to spread everything from local news and developments, to job opportunities and the latest school dinner menus by the local government. On the other side, Jun residents will book appointments with doctors, lodge complaints about local services, report crimes, and generally become involved in the local community.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.digitaltrends.com\u002Fsocial-media\u002Ftwitter-reaches-300-million-active-users-investor-expectations-not-met\u002F\"\u003ETwitter now has 300 million users\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not just about basic communication either. Mayor Rodriguez Salas is frequently active though \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002FJoseantonioJun\"\u003Ehis own account\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. All the town&#x2019;s public services have their own Twitter account, as does the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002FPoliciaJUN\"\u003Epolice force\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, even though there is only one police officer. The squad car has the Twitter account painted on the body, and seemingly everywhere one looks, the Twitter bird logo can be seen. Even the guy who drives the street sweeper is a Twitter user, and is known for his \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002FBarredoraJun\"\u003Echeery and amusing messages\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which he posts along with before and after shots of his best work.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDoes any of this social networking make a difference to the way Jun operates? According to a report published by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.independent.co.uk\u002Flife-style\u002Fgadgets-and-tech\u002Ffeatures\u002Fthe-town-that-runs-on-twitter-juns-residents-tweet-to-report-crime-and-chat-to-their-mayor-10248167.html\"\u003EThe Independent\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, things work very well. It gives the example of a resident tweeting a photo showing a broken streetlamp, which was repaired three-and-a-half minutes later. That&#x2019;s faster than it would take many of us to change a bulb in our own homes. Jun doesn&#x2019;t leave its older citizens out of all this either, and has a special program for those over 65 years old to learn about social media and how to use the Internet.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe mayor is says Twitter helps bring residents and government closer together, and that where before town employees weren&#x2019;t recognized for work in the community, are now appreciated, which means people take more pride in their work. Law enforcement also benefits from an improved image, and can react faster thanks to reports coming through faster, and usually with photos that include the exact location.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EResearchers at MIT&#x2019;s Laboratory for Social Machines are now studying Jun and its method of virtual governance &#x2014; which is believed to be the only one of its type in the world &#x2014; to see if the project can be implemented on a larger scale elsewhere.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E","content_status":"UNPUBLISHED","td_applet_infos":[],"canonical_urls":[],"uploaded_images":[],"type":"story","wiki_ids":["Twitter","Local_government","Local_news"],"yct_categories":["yct:001000085"],"privateTags":[],"leadImages":[{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w175\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":175,"height":117,"size_type":"175","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w175\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w200\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":200,"height":133,"size_type":"200","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w200\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w250\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":250,"height":167,"size_type":"250","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w250\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":300,"height":200,"size_type":"300","formats":{},"types":{"image\u002Fjpeg":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w300\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg"}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w350\u002F182e99d9a0cdcb3d197e7dd6da871cb404a1860d.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":350,"height":233,"size_typ
